The British Film Institute (BFI) announced that box office revenue increased by 17% to £1.24 billion in 2015 compared to the previous year. Cinema admissions also rose by 9%, reaching 171.9 million tickets sold. Film production spending reached £1.41 billion, the second-highest amount ever recorded. This marks the first year since 2012 that both admissions and box office revenue have increased. Five films surpassed £40 million at the UK box office in 2015, compared to only one film, The Hobbit: The Desolation of Smaug, in 2014. The Force Awakens, released in December, grossed £114 million, becoming the UK's most successful film of all time. Spectre, the latest James Bond film, was second with £94.7 million, followed by Jurassic World with £64.5 million. The Avengers: Age of Ultron earned £48.3 million and Minions secured fifth place with £47.7 million. The BFI also reported that UK independent films captured an 11% market share in 2015, the third-highest on record. Eight independent films earned over £5 million at the box office. Tom Hardy's Legend, in which he portrayed the Kray twins, was the highest-grossing independent film with £18.4 million. The Second Best Exotic Marigold Hotel came in second place with £16 million. The UK's film production spend decreased by 6% from 2014's record total of £1.49 billion, a year that saw the production of films like The Force Awakens and Age of Ultron. Amanda Nevill, chief executive of the BFI, stated, "With film production spending exceeding £1.4 billion, audiences flocking to cinemas, and UK box office revenue surpassing £1.2 billion for the first time, today's figures demonstrate the continued golden age of British film and underscore film's significant contribution to the UK economy. It's noteworthy that a diverse range of outstanding British independent films captured the hearts and minds of audiences in a highly competitive year, but it's evident that the market remains challenging for independent and specialized film makers and distributors." Culture minister Ed Vaizey celebrated the figures as "great news."

Shelly-Ann Fraser-Pryce, her Jamaican teammate, finished third in 10.86, failing to become the first woman to win three consecutive gold medals in the event. Thompson expressed her surprise at her victory, saying she didn't know how to celebrate when she crossed the finish line. Fraser-Pryce, while disappointed with her result, emphasized the importance of Jamaica retaining the 100m title. Philip, while acknowledging her below-par performance, remained focused on the positive aspects of her Olympic experience.
A convoy of buses and ambulances arrived in Zabadani to transport fighters and some civilians to Beirut. This evacuation is part of a truce agreed upon in September, which covers Zabadani and two towns in the north that had been besieged by rebel forces. Approximately 300 families from these towns are also receiving safe passage. On Monday, at least 14 people were killed and 90 injured in two suicide bombings in the central city of Homs. The blasts occurred in the Zahraa neighborhood, which is predominantly inhabited by members of the Alawite sect, to which President Bashar al-Assad belongs. Zabadani had been under siege by pro-government forces supported by the Lebanese Shia militant group Hezbollah. Conversely, the towns of Kefraya and Fuaa, in the northern province of Idlib, were under siege by Sunni rebels. Families from Kefraya and Fuaa are being taken to Turkey and then to Lebanon. The International Committee for the Red Cross (ICRC) stated that the Lebanese Red Cross, the Syrian Arab Red Crescent, and the UN are all involved in the operation. Monday's evacuations are the latest in a series of similar actions. Zabadani is the last major rebel stronghold along the Lebanese border. Rebel fighters had been holding out but faced almost certain defeat. Localized ceasefires were at one point proposed as a potential way to end the bloodshed and stalemate, but correspondents say they have failed to gain any real traction.

Susan Curtis, 67, from Buckinghamshire, and Michael James, 77, from Dorset, who were passengers in the Audi, died as a result of the crash. An investigation by the Liberal Democrats revealed that over 11,000 people waited more than 10 days for a specialist appointment since 2013. Party leader Kirsty Williams expressed concern over the situation, calling it "shocking and disappointing." A Welsh Government spokesperson stated that more people are surviving the disease despite an increase in diagnoses. The target is for 95% of patients initially suspected of having cancer to begin definitive treatment within 62 days of diagnosis. In June 2013, Health Minister Mark Drakeford emphasized the importance of patients receiving their first hospital appointment within 10 days of referral to reach this target. The Welsh Government reported that over 22,000 people were referred by their GP with suspected breast cancer between October 2013 and September 2015, with 2,249 diagnosed and 92.3% of them starting definitive treatment within 62 days. While Betsi Cadwaladr and Cardiff and Vale health boards did not provide specific details, Betsi Cadwaladr stated that the average wait for a cancer specialist appointment at Ysbyty Glan Clwyd and Ysbyty Gwynedd was 21 days. Powys Teaching health board refers its patients to hospitals in neighboring health boards, with the latest figures for the three months to December showing that 83.7% of cancer patients started treatment within 62 days. Ms. Williams stressed the urgency of the situation, highlighting the emotional toll on patients and the need to address the systemic capacity issues within cancer services. A Welsh Government spokesperson emphasized that one-stop diagnostic clinics, held concurrently with the first outpatient appointment, allow for immediate treatment for many women referred with suspected breast cancer. An Aneurin Bevan health board spokesperson reported a reduction in waiting times from referral to clinic appointment to 19 days in the last three months, ensuring all patients with suspected malignancy are seen and treated within 62 days, meeting the Welsh Government's target.

Two children were among those whose bodies were recovered from the capsized boat. Two survivors, including a pregnant woman, were rescued. They stated there were 20 to 25 people on board. Since 2015, hundreds have died attempting the crossing from Turkey to Greece. After a deal between Turkey and the EU in March 2022, numbers dropped significantly. However, there are concerns that crossings may increase if the agreement is weakened due to strained relations. Greek and Turkish coastguard officials reported the recovery of six women, a child, and two men in Greek waters, while six men and a child were found in Turkish waters. The survivors said the boat overturned on Sunday night. Philippe Leclerc, the Greece representative for the UN's refugee agency UNHCR, emphasized the ongoing risks despite the decline in crossings. In a separate incident, an Iranian man died during a police pursuit near the Greek-Turkish border after a van carrying migrants overturned.
The budget for the two events was initially £9.29 billion but has been revised to £8.77 billion, representing a £151 million saving since October. This decrease is due to reduced spending on policing, security, transport, and construction. Sports Minister Hugh Robertson attributed this to the sound financial management of all parties involved. These figures were released in a written statement to Parliament by Minister for Sport Robertson following the publication of the London Organizing Committee of the Olympic and Paralympic Games (Locog)'s final report and accounts in May. The original budget was set in 2007, nearly four times the estimated cost when London bid in 2005. It was subsequently increased to account for unforeseen costs such as VAT, heightened security measures, and an expanded plan to regenerate the Lower Lea Valley area. As the one-year anniversary of the London 2012 Games approaches, Robertson expressed national pride and highlighted the progress made in establishing a lasting legacy. He noted the ongoing transformation of the Olympic Park, with the long-term future secured for all eight major venues and the first residents moving into the Olympic Village in the summer. The Olympic Development Agency is converting the Olympic Village apartments into thousands of new homes by removing partitions and installing kitchens. This project is expected to be completed by the end of the summer, with the entire transformation finished by 2014. Temporary Games venues are also being returned to their original owners and purposes.
The Ministry of Justice confirmed that the Grade II listed prison, closed in 2013, would be used as a venue for the town's 2016 Year of Culture events. The Year of Culture aims to unite the town's arts groups and establish it as a cultural destination. Alex Brennan, of organizers Reading UK, stated it would be a "fabulous" addition to the Year of Culture program. The MoJ said it would collaborate with a third party to make the venue suitable for hosting a season of art, literature, and music in the autumn. They emphasized there would be no additional cost to taxpayers. Reading East MP Rob Wilson expressed that using the prison would "help celebrate the town's cultural and historical significance." Mr. Brennan added, "It has a central place in Reading's history. It would be a marvelous and rather unusual venue, and I really hope something comes of it." The prison was the subject of inmate Oscar Wilde's poem, "The Ballad of Reading Gaol," and part of the prison is located on the site of a Scheduled Ancient Monument. Notable inmates include Roderick Maclean, who shot Queen Victoria in 1882, Amelia Dyer, convicted of baby farming murders in 1896, Oscar Wilde, the playwright jailed after an 1895 trial for indecency, and Arthur Griffith, a leading Irish republican interned in 1916. In November 2015, the MoJ announced the site would be sold for housing. A spokesperson confirmed archaeological investigations were scheduled to begin soon before a development plan is created. Reading Borough Council hopes to take over the site and has previously criticized the MoJ for "dithering" about making a decision regarding its long-term future. The empty jail cost the MoJ approximately £262,000 in the 2014/15 financial year, covering security and utility bills.
Sgt Craig Nicholas Jones appealed his conviction for speeding, claiming the malfunctioning lights on two 50mph signs on the A55 at Old Colwyn made it impossible to know the speed limit. However, judges at the High Court in London ruled that the signs would have been visible in the unmarked police car's headlights. They reinstated the 90-day driving ban initially imposed by magistrates. Sgt Jones was clocked driving 98mph on April 1, 2009, between Llanddulas and Colwyn Bay. His lawyers argued that the broken lights on the speed limit signs meant he should not have been convicted, citing a policy at the time against enforcing speed limits when signs were malfunctioning. The judges disagreed, stating that a decision not to prosecute Sgt Jones would have damaged public trust in the justice system. They emphasized that the signs, despite the broken lights, were correctly placed and followed all regulations. The judges concluded that the signs were clearly visible in the car's headlights and that minor breaches of regulations do not invalidate speed limits. Sgt Jones's appeal was dismissed, and the 90-day driving ban will now take effect on January 31st.

Deborah Streatfield of MyBigCareer considers it unjust that students aspiring to study medicine are required to pay for work experience to bolster their university applications. This paid work experience is offered through the Chartwell Trust, which manages a private hospital in Essex. The trust's directors describe the opportunity as "remarkable," stating that the "Chartwell Work Experience For Medical School Applications" provides an in-depth understanding of hospital and healthcare environments. Students will shadow staff and gain valuable medical experience to support their Ucas applications. The brochure, targeted at students aged 15 and above, assures "good supervision from motivated staff" in the hospital and "interview training conducted by our qualified doctors." The trust also operates care homes, and the brochure mentions rotations through these facilities, which cater to children with learning difficulties and elderly individuals with dementia. Medicine is highly competitive for university admission, and the work placement program claims to teach students valuable medical school interview techniques. Streatfield's charity aims to provide young people with better career guidance, believing that improved social mobility stems from greater awareness of available options. However, she argues that selling work experience in this manner creates a barrier to accessing sought-after courses like medicine. Streatfield emphasizes that work experience is crucial for medical applications and that disadvantaged students often lack family connections to leverage. She finds this scheme fundamentally unfair. MyBigCareer plans to pilot unpaid work experience placements with 43 GP practices in Hackney and the City of London. In a statement, Chartwell Trust Care's directors assert that the placement offers one-on-one meetings with senior management, consultant physicians, surgeons, and directors, providing insight into healthcare. They emphasize the "remarkable opportunity" afforded by the company's diagnostic facilities, outpatient clinics, and care homes, stating that the empathy and compassion students experience contribute to their personal development. They clarify that the fee covers administrative costs and individual coaching designed to boost confidence and self-esteem for healthcare career applications. Concerns have been raised about attracting a more diverse applicant pool to medicine, with warnings that it attracts too many recruits from affluent backgrounds. Research from the Medical Schools Council in December revealed that half of UK secondary schools and colleges had not sent a single applicant to medicine in recent years.

On Sunday, some passengers were trapped in the Starflyer ride's capsules for over three hours. Firefighters from London Fire Brigade had to carefully access each cage individually due to the ride's structure. A technical fault caused the ride to stop. Dannorthover, a Twitter user who was rescued, expressed gratitude to the London Fire Brigade. Two fire engines and two cherry picker ladders were dispatched to the scene, where engineers worked on the ride. Despite the lengthy wait, passengers remained calm. The London Fire Brigade confirmed no injuries and received the call shortly before 6 pm GMT. The Starflyer, a 60-meter-high ride located at London Wonderground, was shut down for investigation. London Wonderground acknowledged the technical fault and stated that everyone on the ride was safely evacuated. They are collaborating with the ride's management company to determine the cause. The Southbank Centre expressed appreciation to the firefighters for their assistance and pledged to work with the ride owners to investigate the fault. The ride will remain closed until the investigation is complete. The Starflyer has previously appeared at London Wonderground and Winter Wonderland in Hyde Park.
Cambridgeshire police released photos of poorly parked bicycles in Cambridge to encourage people to park more responsibly. The force stated that these scenes are common and part of their #badlyparkedbike campaign. Cycling is popular in Cambridge, with 58% of residents cycling at least monthly. Inspector Matt Johnson explained that while the images are shocking, they reflect a recurring issue. He emphasized that inconsiderate parking obstructs walkways, hinders others from accessing their bikes, and has even resulted in injuries. Johnson recommended using designated bike racks, which, when paired with a good lock, deter theft. Public response to the campaign was mixed. Some users deemed bad parking dangerous, while others pointed out the need for more bike racks. One user, Al Storer, argued that the photos simply highlight areas with insufficient parking. Inspector Johnson acknowledged the city's extensive cycle parking provision but stressed the ongoing challenge of abandoned bikes occupying valuable spaces.
The UK's Intellectual Property Office (IPO) supported Swatch's opposition, filed in March 2014, arguing that "iWatch" was too close to its "iSwatch" and "Swatch" trademarks. Apple ultimately named its smartwatch "Apple Watch" when it launched in 2015. However, Apple can now use "iWatch" in the UK for specific products, such as computer software and accessories, but not for hardware, monitors, audio/video devices, or cameras. This decision followed an April hearing. Trademark lawyer Sharon Daboul from EIP law firm stated, "This decision highlights the challenges global brands face when launching new products internationally." She explained that trademarks are country-specific, requiring registration in each target market. Daboul added that not securing the "iWatch" trademark globally likely influenced Apple's decision to choose a different name for its smartwatch. Swatch declined to comment.
Following road closures in Denbighshire and Chirk, Infrastructure and Economy Secretary Ken Skates has requested reports with recommendations to address the issue. The A55 in Denbighshire was shut in both directions after a tractor overturned on Friday. Due to the extent of the damage, the road remained closed until Tuesday morning after resurfacing. Separately, a crash on the Ceiriog viaduct on Monday closed the A5 at Chirk. While the southbound carriageway has reopened, the northbound lane will remain closed until at least Friday while temporary barriers are installed. Delays in securing specialists for this work, Mr. Skates explained, are due to their current involvement in projects including barrier installation in London following recent incidents there. Officials will review the response to road damage, explore improvements, and assess associated costs. Acknowledging public criticism regarding the severity of delays caused by these incidents, Mr. Skates stated, "There are clearly lessons to be learned."

The 110-acre park, owned by North Lincolnshire Council, is home to many deer. Daphne had become accustomed to visitors near the center after being fed. Joanne Coates, a photographer, has spent three years documenting the lives of Scottish fishermen. Her work is inspired by her childhood trips to the seaside with her brother. These photographs depict the harsh realities of their work, including long days, difficult conditions, and the ever-present danger. The fishing industry is a dangerous one, with more lives lost in the first half of 2016 than in the entirety of the previous year. The Fishermen's Mission estimates that an average of 15 fishermen are killed or seriously injured annually. Coates' images focus on the inshore fishermen of the Orkney Fishermen's Society, a cooperative established in 1953. Their primary catch consists of brown crab and lobster. The society works collaboratively with researchers to ensure sustainable fishing practices, and the area is home to Europe's largest lobster hatchery, which releases over 100,000 lobsters each year. Coates' photographs capture the daily routines of these men as they face an uncertain future.

Dennis and Doreen Green, aged 81 and 80 respectively, tragically died in a two-car collision on April 5th near York. The couple, from Strensall, were described as beloved parents, grandparents, and great-grandparents. Their family, in a statement, expressed their profound grief, saying they would be deeply missed. Relatives shared that the Greens enjoyed sequence dancing, frequent holidays, and an active social life. They were well-known and respected in their village of over 50 years, and their loss would be felt by many. The family noted that they had celebrated their 60th wedding anniversary the day before the accident and a family gathering was planned for the weekend. They expressed the immense void their absence would create but found solace in cherished memories and the comfort of their enduring love. The crash occurred around 1:20 PM BST on Northgate Lane. Dennis Green was driving their Citroen Xsara, with Doreen as a passenger, when it collided with a Land Rover Defender traveling in the opposite direction. The 20-something Land Rover driver received minor treatment at the scene.
The Hamilton Band, established in 1856 and one of Northern Ireland's oldest, served as the regimental band for the 10th battalion of the Royal Inniskilling Fusiliers. They provided morale-boosting concerts and even used their bass drum as a communion table during the Battle of the Somme. Tragically, Lance Corporal Joseph Scott from Moore Street and Rifleman George Mills from Pine Street lost their lives on July 1st, 1916, just the beginning of the heavy casualties that would follow. After the war, surviving members rebuilt the band, facing the challenge of replacing most of their instruments, which had been taken to the front. Eventually, the original drums were returned, including the bass drum, which is now displayed in St Columb's Cathedral Chapter House. Ian Bartlett, the cathedral's curator, explained that this drum was used throughout World War I, including for Sunday communion services on the battlefield. The band reformed after the war and used the drum until the 1970s when it was donated to the cathedral. Robert McGonagle, secretary of the Hamilton Flute Band, praised the courage and dedication of those who served, questioning if such commitment would be seen today. To honor those who died, a remembrance ceremony will be held at Derry's war memorial, along with a special drum service at St Columb's Cathedral to recognize the band's contributions.

A presidential spokesman told the BBC that it was too early to blame anyone for the killing of General Adolphe Nshimirimana, who was attacked by rockets and gunfire. Mr. Nkurunziza won a third term last month amidst deadly protests over his decision to run again. Opponents argued that this violated the constitution, and a coup attempt occurred in May. Thierry Vircoulon, an International Crisis Group analyst, told BBC Afrique that Nshimirimana, although not officially, was the regime's number two, and his assassination is a serious blow to Burundi's government. Witnesses reported that four men in military uniform fired on the general's car with machine guns and rocket launchers in Bujumbura's Kamenge district. Presidential spokesperson Gerve Abehayo refuted suggestions that the attack could have been carried out by members of Burundi's security forces. He stated that the government maintains support, the army remains strong and united, and the killing of one general does not mean the entire military has been eradicated. President Nkurunziza has requested that the investigation into the general's death be completed within a week. The African Union, European Union, and the US have all condemned the attack. AU chairperson Nkosazana Dlamini Zuma described it as a "barbaric act" that likely further destabilizes the country. Burundian journalist Esdras Ndikumana, who works for AFP and Radio France Internationale, reported being detained and beaten by intelligence officers after attempting to photograph the attack site. Since the unrest began in April, over 70 people have been killed, and 180,000 have fled the country, according to the UN refugee agency. Mr. Nkurunziza came to power in 2005 after a 12-year conflict between ethnic Hutus and Tutsis that resulted in 300,000 deaths.
The entertainer and former husband of Liza Minelli passed away earlier this month at the age of 62. Celebrities such as Cleo Rocos, Kerry Katona, Denise Welch, Christopher Maloney, Vanessa Feltz, and Kym Marsh attended his funeral. It was confirmed that a tour announced by Gest before his death will proceed as planned in July. The lyrics to Nat King Cole's "Unforgettable" were featured in a white floral arrangement on his coffin, accompanied by a musical note and a butterfly. Dean Gaffney, Kristina Rihanoff, and Danniella Westbrook were also among the mourners. The tour's name originated from a misunderstanding on this year's Celebrity Big Brother, where Gest was a contestant. Angie Bowie mistakenly informed fellow housemate Tiffany Pollard that David Bowie had died. Pollard, believing Gest, who was unwell at the time, had passed away, became distressed. The "Alive With Soul" tour comprises nine dates, starting on July 1st at York's Barbican Centre and concluding on July 13th in Nottingham. Gest's friend Imad Handi, who has co-produced Gest's tours for several years, stated: "He may sadly be gone, but his spirit lives on in the music he loved." Tributes will also be paid to singer Billy Paul, who was originally scheduled to perform but died earlier this week. Freda Payne, known for her hit song "Band of Gold," will be the compere for the concerts. Handi noted that the concerts will provide fans with an opportunity to pay their respects and celebrate Gest's life. He added that the artists were devastated by Gest's death and felt compelled to proceed with the tour as a way to remember him through their music. Gest died at the Four Seasons hotel in Canary Wharf, London, earlier this month at the age of 62.
Facing strong opposition from business groups and oil companies, Governor Jerry Brown and other lawmakers removed a proposal to reduce petroleum use in vehicles by 50% by 2030 from a climate change bill. The proposal's supporters, including State Senate leader Kevin de Leon, accused oil firms of using scare tactics to deter lawmakers. Despite this setback, Governor Brown expressed his commitment to advancing other climate change reforms, such as increasing renewable electricity use and improving energy efficiency in buildings. He stated that while oil companies may have won this particular battle, they have lost the larger war. Catherine Reheis-Boyd, president of the Western States Petroleum Association, praised the decision to remove the emissions target, emphasizing the interconnectedness of California's energy future, economic competitiveness, and environment. California, the second-largest producer of carbon dioxide from fossil fuels among US states, remains focused on addressing climate change. Governor Brown plans to continue pushing for the remaining components of the climate change bill and will attend the United Nations climate change conference in Paris.

Brain Injury Matters expressed uncertainty about the number of children with brain injuries due to the absence of a dedicated unit. Early detection is crucial as symptoms may not be immediately apparent, gradually developing as the brain matures. Janet McCullough's son, Eric, experienced a kidney infection that progressed to encephalitis, causing brain swelling. Despite receiving antibiotics, his body attacked his brain, leading to headaches, light sensitivity, and illness. After hospitalization, Eric emerged as a changed child. A year later, his family works with Brain Injury Matters to raise awareness. Janet noted that Eric tires easily, both physically and mentally, lacks a sense of time, and struggles with dyslexia and concentration. Acquired brain injury is more common due to medical advancements that reduce mortality. It can result from various causes, including accidents, falls, infections, oxygen deprivation, or strokes. While it can affect all ages, it's most prevalent in young children up to four years old, teenagers and young adults aged 15 to 29, and males. Fiona McCabe, CEO of Brain Injury Matters, stated that the charity is assisting more families. Based on UK evidence and anecdotal information, they estimate up to 1,000 new cases of childhood brain injury annually in Northern Ireland. Lack of precise data hinders resource allocation. Eric's family receives support from Brain Injury Matters and the Child Brain Injury Trust, which helps them manage the adjustments brought by Eric's changed condition.

The parliament's Budgetary Control Committee is investigating allowances given to Martin Schulz's advisor, Markus Engels. Engels was reportedly allowed to claim Brussels as his residence while living in Berlin in 2012. Schulz's SPD party declined to comment to the BBC but stated to German magazines Spiegel and Stern that travel arrangements like Engels' were "normal practice" in Brussels. The EU anti-fraud office Olaf, which previously investigated Marine Le Pen's expenses, is examining media reports about the employment conditions of "certain European Parliament staff members." Olaf will analyze the reports to determine if they fall under its jurisdiction and if there is "sufficient suspicion of fraud, corruption or any illegal activity affecting the EU's financial interests" to warrant an investigation. Schulz led the European Parliament from 2012 until this year, when he stepped down to run for the German general election. Engels now manages Schulz's campaign. In January 2012, Schulz requested that the European Parliament's Director-General for Communication authorize a "long-term mission" for Engels to support his activities as EP president in Berlin. The Budgetary Control Committee is questioning why Brussels was chosen as Engels' place of employment, which entitled him to daily allowances and an expat allowance despite no travel costs occurring. The committee also wants to know who made the decision and how Engels was selected for the position. A formal response is expected next month.
Hundreds of fans attended a memorial service for David Bowie at London's Union Chapel. The 69-year-old musician, who died from cancer on January 10th, was honored with a performance of his music by various artists, including The Magic Numbers and Glen Matlock of the Sex Pistols. Bowie's death came two days after the release of his album *Blackstar*. Since then, tribute concerts have been held worldwide, and many of his songs have re-entered the UK charts. Fans filled the chapel, where Bowie's most famous songs, played on an organ, filled the air. A large screen displayed images of Bowie throughout his career, and the event began with a mass sing-along of "Starman." Maggi Ronson, sister of Bowie's late guitarist Mick Ronson, performed "Ziggy Stardust" with The Featherz, praising Bowie's "massive influence." Guy Pratt, a former bassist for Pink Floyd and Roxy Music, called Bowie the "greatest artist I've known in my lifetime" before performing "Life on Mars" with members of The Feeling. The five-hour concert, streamed live on YouTube, featured a mix of Bowie's hits, clips of his interviews and music videos, and tributes from journalists, authors, and those who worked with him. There were also unique musical moments, such as "Where Are We Now?" played on a saw and "Wild Is the Wind" performed on a harp. The dimly-lit chapel, adorned with flowers and candles, is a working church and music venue. A wall of remembrance allowed fans, many wearing Bowie's signature Aladdin Sane lightning bolt, to share personal tributes and messages. Comedian David Baddiel addressed the audience, stating, "I assumed Bowie was immortal. I thought he was a space god who had come to live amongst us. And I couldn't process that he had died... He is, was, the greatest tunesmith we have." Organizers described the event as an opportunity for those inspired by Bowie's work to pay tribute. Neil Lindsay, one of the organizers, said it was "for fans by fans." He added, "He's been around all our lives but he's still as relevant and interesting now. You can't say that about all artists who become legends. He was still innovating even in the way he said goodbye." Tickets were priced at £4 to cover the event's costs, and a collection for Macmillan Cancer
Southport dismissed Andy Bishop following a poor run of four losses in their last five matches. Despite this, they displayed defensive strength under Burr, resisting Eastleigh's attacks in the first half. Eastleigh maintained pressure after halftime and were rewarded in the 51st minute when Mikael Mandron scored with a curled shot after a half-cleared cross. Eastleigh continued to control the game but failed to score again, allowing James Gray to equalize almost immediately after coming on as a substitute, converting James Caton's cross in the 71st minute.
Teachers from Llandrindod High School demonstrated at county hall, carrying banners and chanting slogans. The National Union of Teachers (NUT) stated the strike was in support of children whose right to a quality education is being jeopardized. Powys council's schools cabinet member, Arwel Jones, expressed disappointment in the union's actions. The council is currently reviewing plans to restructure secondary schools in the mid and south regions. Councillor Jones asserted that schools are encountering significant difficulties and that strike action would not deter their program but could hinder student progress during a critical period. Nineteen Powys schools have been impacted by the strike, with six fully closed and thirteen partially closed. NUT organizer Cai Jones described the march turnout as "wonderful," noting the participation of parents and children. He stated that the community showed strong support as they marched through the town center, with people leaving their shops to show solidarity and drivers honking their horns in encouragement. The teachers presented a list of demands to Powys council at county hall and convened at Llandrindod Pavilion afterward to discuss the desired changes.
Eleven care workers will be sentenced for mistreating and neglecting five patients at Winterbourne View. A BBC investigation also uncovered evidence of alleged abuse against former patient Ben Pullar. The National Autistic Society called for a full investigation, but police declined to reopen the case. Mr. Pullar, who is autistic and bipolar with severe learning difficulties, spent almost a year at Winterbourne View in 2009. The nurse involved, Maxwell Nyamukapa, was suspended and later reinstated. Despite attempts to contact him, Mr. Nyamukapa has refused to comment. Police classified the incident as assault, stating the nurse acted instinctively in self-defense. Sarah Lambert from the National Autistic Society emphasized the need for full investigations into any serious injuries sustained by disabled individuals in residential care. She condemned the abuse of those with autism and other disabilities by caregivers as abhorrent and a hate crime. Lambert urged police to reopen the case to send a clear message that such abuse by support staff is unacceptable and a serious offense. Care notes from Mr. Pullar's time at the hospital mention an incident involving his teeth weeks after his arrival. His family was informed he had "bitten the floor," leading to a visit to Bristol Dental Hospital where the alarm was raised. Notes obtained by Inside Out West indicate the nurse was bitten and retaliated to remove his fingers. South Gloucestershire Council declined to comment on Mr. Pullar's case. Castlebeck, the hospital's former owner, stated its new management was thoroughly reviewing events at Winterbourne View and had referred Mr. Nyamukapa twice to the Nursing & Midwifery Council, which declined to comment.

Coyle believes the player has the potential to become a Premier League player, comparing him to Sam Gallagher and Tommie Hoban, the types of players he would invest in. Gallagher made 18 Premier League appearances for Southampton in the 2013-14 season, scoring in a victory over Norwich. However, a serious knee injury hampered his progress, and he failed to score in 15 loan games at MK Dons last season. Coyle expressed his desire to sign Gallagher permanently, along with Hoban. He highlighted the young player's willingness to learn and his efforts to impart experience and knowledge.
Denis Pitner, a Croatian official, was banned from tennis for a year in August due to sharing player fitness information and accessing a betting account. Despite the ban, Pitner was approved by the US Open on July 13th and received his credential before the USTA was informed. The USTA, acknowledging a "flaw in our process," stated they were shocked to learn Pitner officiated at the 2015 US Open as a linesman after the Guardian newspaper revealed the information. This incident follows recent reports by the BBC and Buzzfeed alleging widespread match-fixing in tennis. In response, tennis governing bodies announced an independent review panel to investigate corruption claims, a process expected to take at least a year. Pitner also officiated at the January ATP Qatar Open in Doha. The USTA pledged to cooperate with the review panel to prevent future occurrences and emphasized the seriousness of the matter, prioritizing an investigation into the error.
In March, North Wales Fire and Rescue Authority postponed plans to eliminate one of Wrexham's fire engines until after the May elections. The new authority hasn't ruled out the cut as it develops its budget for the next three years. Deputy Chief Fire Officer Dawn Docx stated that any cuts would be a last resort. While there are no proposals to reduce front-line services, the Fire Brigades Union (FBU) is concerned that the engine will be targeted again as the authority addresses budget constraints. Cerith Griffiths, representing the FBU, expressed that the cut would force firefighters to disregard safety protocols to save lives. The service's safety guidelines dictate the number of crews required for specific incidents. For house fires, two fire engines are necessary. Mr. Griffiths explained that without the second engine, firefighters would be compelled to either delay crucial minutes or enter a burning building without backup, jeopardizing their own safety. He compared the situation to the Grenfell fire in London, where firefighters exceeded protocols. Mr. Griffiths emphasized that waiting half an hour for a second engine could be detrimental in a time-sensitive situation. He believes that such a delay would endanger lives. Earlier proposals to eliminate one of Wrexham's two fire engines and 24 firefighter positions to address a £900,000 funding gap by 2020 were withdrawn in March following public opposition. The station is the only one in north Wales with three fire engines - two full-time and one part-time. The new authority is currently formulating its budget plans and gathering public feedback before releasing its draft financial strategy in November. Ms. Docx stated that no proposals have been made, but the service is exploring cost-saving measures that won't affect front-line jobs. She acknowledged that a fire engine might be removed from a station, potentially leading to longer wait times for backup. Ms. Docx stressed that this is not a desired outcome for senior fire officers and that if budget constraints necessitate such a decision, it would be a last resort considered by the authority.
Vandals spray-painted "f*** law" in red on a National Park Service monument early Tuesday morning. Crews are using a safe paint stripper to remove the graffiti. US Civil War memorials have become a focal point in discussions about race in the US. Additional, unreadable graffiti was found in silver paint on a nearby sign directing tourists to the Smithsonian Institution. President Lincoln led the Union government to victory over the Confederacy and issued the Emancipation Proclamation in 1863, freeing enslaved African Americans. He was assassinated in Washington five days after General Robert E. Lee surrendered, ending the war. The statue of General Lee became a source of controversy over the weekend when white supremacists and anti-racist protesters clashed in Charlottesville, Virginia, over its removal. A protester died after being struck by a car, and President Donald Trump faced criticism for not immediately blaming the violence on white supremacist groups. Following a 2015 hate attack in South Carolina where a man used the Confederate flag to express his racist views, many cities across the US have sought to remove statues of Confederate leaders, including Charlottesville. After the violence in Charlottesville, several more cities announced plans to remove their Confederate monuments. Baltimore, Lexington, Memphis, and Jacksonville have all proposed removing controversial monuments. On Monday, protesters in Durham, North Carolina, toppled a bronze statue of a Confederate leader while police recorded the event. Durham County Sheriff Mike Andrews stated that police are reviewing the video to identify and prosecute those responsible for removing the 1924 statue.
A Protestant mother of ten from east Belfast, she converted to Catholicism upon marrying Arthur McConville. After facing intimidation in east Belfast, the family relocated to west Belfast and resided in the Divis Flats on the Lower Falls Road. Her husband passed away in 1971. In December 1972, the IRA removed her from her home. Speculation arose that she was taken after neighbors observed her assisting an injured British soldier. Some alleged she was an informer, but an investigation by the Northern Ireland Police Ombudsman refuted this claim. In a recent BBC documentary, one of Mrs. McConville's daughters, Agnes, recounted her mother's abduction for the first time, describing hearing her mother's screams as she was taken by men and women and forced into a van, marking the last time they saw her. It is believed she was held in several locations before being killed. Her disappearance initially received significant media attention, especially leading up to Christmas, with her children pleading for information. However, within the community, republicans disseminated the message that she was simply "lying low," causing her story to gradually fade from public view. The IRA consistently denied involvement in her disappearance. Jean McConville's case resurfaced in 1999 with the establishment of the Independent Commission for the Location of Victims' Remains. This body, created by the British and Irish governments, aimed to confidentially gather information to locate the remains of those disappeared during the Troubles. The IRA admitted that year to murdering and secretly burying nine of the Disappeared, including Jean McConville. Her remains were finally discovered in 2003 on Shelling Hill Beach in County Louth, Republic of Ireland. Irish police confirmed she died from a gunshot wound to the head. Following the discovery, the IRA issued a statement apologizing for the suffering caused to the families of the Disappeared and acknowledging the prolonged nature of their pain.
